Alvin Drew, Nicole Stott, Eric Boe, Steven Lindsey, Michael Barratt and Steve Bowen\n         <div class="" style="width:100%; text-align:center; border-top:1px #aaa solid">\n          <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">\n           Space Shuttle program\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div style="width:100%">\n          <div class="noprint" style="float: left; text-align:left;padding-right:0.5em;">\n           \xe2\x86\x90\n           <a href="/wiki/STS-132" title="STS-132">\n            STS-132\n           </a>\n          </div>\n          <div class="noprint" style="float: right; text-align:right;padding-left:0.5em;">\n           <a href="/wiki/STS-134" title="STS-134">\n            STS-134\n           </a>\n           \xe2\x86\x92\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        STS-133\n       </b>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_International_Space_Station#Assembly_sequence" title="Assembly of the International Space Station">\n        ISS assembly\n       </a>\n       flight\n       <b>\n        ULF5\n       </b>\n       )\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manifest_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-manifest-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       was the 133rd mission in\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">\n        Space Shuttle program\n       </a>\n       ; during the mission,\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">\n        Space Shuttle\n        <i>\n         Discovery\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       docked with the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       . It was\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       \'s 39th and final mission. The mission launched on 24 February 2011, and landed on 9 March 2011. The crew consisted of six American\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">\n        astronauts\n       </a>\n       , all of whom had been on prior spaceflights, headed by Commander\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steven_W._Lindsey" title="Steven W. Lindsey">\n        Steven Lindsey\n       </a>\n       . The crew joined the long-duration six person crew of\n       <a href="/wiki/Expedition_26" title="Expedition 26">\n        Expedition 26\n       </a>\n       , who were already aboard the space station.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sched_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sched-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       About a month before lift-off, one of the original crew members,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timothy_L._Kopra" title="Timothy L. Kopra">\n        Tim Kopra\n       </a>\n       , was injured in a bicycle accident. He was replaced by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephen_G._Bowen" title="Stephen G. Bowen">\n        Stephen Bowen\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The mission transported several items to the space station, including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_(ISS_module)" title="Leonardo (ISS module)">\n        Permanent Multipurpose Module\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       , which was left permanently docked to one of the station\'s ports. The shuttle also carried the third of four\n       <a href="/wiki/ExPRESS_Logistics_Carrier" title="ExPRESS Logistics Carrier">\n        ExPRESS Logistics Carriers\n       </a>\n       to the ISS, as well as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Humanoid_robot" title="Humanoid robot">\n        humanoid robot\n       </a>\n       called\n       <a href="/wiki/Robonaut" title="Robonaut">\n        Robonaut\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The mission marked both the 133rd flight of the Space Shuttle program and the 39th and final flight of\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       , with the orbiter completing a cumulative total of a whole year (365 days) in space.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The mission was affected by a series of delays due to technical problems with the external tank and, to a lesser extent, the payload. The launch, initially scheduled for September 2010, was pushed back to October, then to November, then finally to February 2011.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n     Terminal countdown demonstration test\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11">\n         <a      <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12">\n           <a href="#Orbital_Maneuvering_System_vapor_leak">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Orbital Maneuvering System vapor leak\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19">\n           <a href="#24_February_.28Flight_Day_1_.E2.80.93_Launch.29">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n   </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24">\n           <a href="#1_March_.28Flight_Day_6_.E2.80.93_PMM_installation.29">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.6\n  </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32">\n           <a href="#9_March_.28Flight_Day_14_.E2.80.93_Re-entry_and_landing.29">\n            <span </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Spacewalks\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34">\n         <a href="#Wake-up_calls">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Wake-up calls\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_payload">\n        Mission payload\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Mission payload">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Permanent_Multipurpose_Module">\n        Permanent Multipurpose Module\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Permanent Multipurpose Module">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Permanent_Multipurpose_Module" title="Permanent Multipurpose Module">\n        Permanent Multipurpose Module\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS_133_PMM_Leonardo.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/STS_133_PMM_Leonardo.jpg/220px-STS_133_PMM_Leonardo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/STS_133_PMM_Leonardo.jpg/330px-STS_133_PMM_Leonardo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/STS_133_PMM_Leonardo.jpg/440px-STS_133_PMM_Leonardo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS_133_PMM_Leonardo.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         PMM\n         <i>\n          Leonardo\n         </i>\n         at the\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Station_Processing_Facility" title="Space Station Processing Facility">\n          Space Station Processing Facility\n         </a>\n         (SSPF).\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       STS-133 left\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       (named after the famed Italian\n       <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">\n        Renaissance\n       </a>\n       inventor\n       <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">\n        Leonardo da Vinci\n       </a>\n       ), one of the three\n       <a href="/wiki/Multi-Purpose_Logistics_Module" title="Multi-Purpose Logistics Module">\n        Multi-Purpose Logistics Modules\n       </a>\n       (MPLMs), on the space station as a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Permanent_Multipurpose_Module" title="Permanent Multipurpose Module">\n        Permanent Multipurpose Module\n       </a>\n       (PMM).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-permanent_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-permanent-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PMM_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PMM-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       PMM\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       added much-needed storage space on the ISS, and was launched with a near-full load of payloads.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The construction of the\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       MPLM by the Italian Space Agency commenced in April 1996. In August 1998, after the completion of primary construction,\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       was delivered to the Kennedy Space Center (KSC). In March 2001,\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       made its first mission on\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       as part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-102" title="STS-102">\n        STS-102\n       </a>\n       flight. The liftoff of\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       inside\n       <i>\n        Discovery\'\n       </i>\n       s payload bay on STS-102 marked the first of seven MPLM flights prior to STS-133.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       With the landing of\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       after the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-131" title="STS-131">\n        STS-131\n       </a>\n       mission,\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       was transferred back to the Space Station Processing Facility at Kennedy Space Center.\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       began receiving modifications and reconfigurations immediately to convert it for permanent attachment to the space station and to facilitate on-orbit maintenance.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some equipment was removed to reduce the overall weight of\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       . These removals resulted in a net weight loss of 178.1\xc2\xa0lb (80.8\xc2\xa0kg). Additional modifications to\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       included the installation of upgraded\n       <a href="/wiki/Multi-layer_insulation" title="Multi-layer insulation">\n        multi-layer insulation\n       </a>\n       (MLI) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Whipple_shield" title="Whipple shield">\n        Micro Meteoroid Orbital Debris\n       </a>\n       (MMOD) shielding to increase the ability of the PMM to handle potential impacts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Micrometeoroid" title="Micrometeoroid">\n        micrometeoroids\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orbital_debris" title="Orbital debris">\n        orbital debris\n       </a>\n       ; a Planar Reflector was installed at the request of the\n       <a href="/wiki/JAXA" title="JAXA">\n        Japanese Space Agency\n       </a>\n       (JAXA).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Following berthing to the space station, the contents of\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       were emptied and moved to appropriate locations on the ISS. Once JAXA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Kounotori_2" title="Kounotori 2">\n        Kounotori 2\n       </a>\n       (HTV-2) arrived in February 2011,\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\'\n       </i>\n       s now-unnecessary launch hardware was transferred to HTV2 for ultimate destruction in Earth\'s atmosphere.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Activities to reconfigure\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       following STS-133 spanned multiple station crew increments.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="ExPRESS_Logistics_Carrier_4">\n        ExPRESS Logistics Carrier 4\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: ExPRESS Logistics Carrier 4">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Express_Logistics_Carrier" title="Express Logistics Carrier">\n        Express Logistics Carrier\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS133_ELC-4.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2000" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/STS133_ELC-4.jpg/140px-STS133_ELC-4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/STS133_ELC-4.jpg/210px-STS133_ELC-4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/STS133_ELC-4.jpg/280px-STS133_ELC-4.jpg 2x" width="140"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS133_ELC-4.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         ELC-4 being lifted from its work stand in the SSPF.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ELC-4_STS-133_Launch_Config.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="308" data-file-width="591" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/ELC-4_STS-133_Launch_Config.jpg/220px-ELC-4_STS-133_Launch_Config.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/ELC-4_STS-133_Launch_Config.jpg/330px-ELC-4_STS-133_Launch_Config.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/ELC-4_STS-133_Launch_Config.jpg/440px-ELC-4_STS-133_Launch_Config.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ELC-4_STS-133_Launch_Config.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         ELC-4 in its launch configuration\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Express_Logistics_Carrier" title="Express Logistics Carrier">\n        Express Logistics Carrier\n       </a>\n       (ELC) is a platform designed to support external payloads mounted to the space station starboard and port trusses with either deep space or Earthward views. On STS-133,\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       carried the ELC-4 to the station to be positioned on the starboard 3 (S3) truss\' lower inboard passive attachment system (PAS). The total weight of the ELC-4 is approximately 8,235 pounds.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Express Logistics Carrier 4 (ELC-4) carried several Orbital Replacement Units (ORUs). Among these were a Heat Rejection System Radiator (HRSR) Flight Support Equipment (FSE), which takes up one whole side of the ELC. The other primary ORUs were the ExPRESS Pallet Controller Avionics 4 (ExPCA #4). The HRSR launching on ELC4 was a spare, if needed, for one of the six radiators that are part of the station\'s external active thermal control system.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Robonaut2">\n        Robonaut2\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Robonaut2">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Robonaut" title="Robonaut">\n        Robonaut\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS133_Crew_and_Robonaut2.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2218" height="298" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/STS133_Crew_and_Robonaut2.jpg/220px-STS133_Crew_and_Robonaut2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/STS133_Crew_and_Robonaut2.jpg/330px-STS133_Crew_and_Robonaut2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/STS133_Crew_and_Robonaut2.jpg/440px-STS133_Crew_and_Robonaut2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS133_Crew_and_Robonaut2.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Robonaut2 and STS-133 crew members pose for a picture near a Destiny lab trainer. (Photo includes original crew member Tim Kopra, who was later replaced by Stephen Bowen)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       carried the\n       <a href="/wiki/Humanoid_robot" title="Humanoid robot">\n        humanoid robot\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Robonaut#Latest_design_.28R2.29" title="Robonaut">\n        Robonaut2\n       </a>\n       (also known as R2) to the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       (ISS). The microgravity conditions aboard the space station provide an ideal opportunity for robots like R2 to work with astronauts. Although the robot\'s primary initial task is teaching engineers how dexterous robots behave in space, it may eventually, through upgrades and advancements, assist spacewalking astronauts to perform scientific work once it has been verified as functional on the space station.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robonaut_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-robonaut-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It was the first humanoid robot in space, and was stowed on board the\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       PMM. Once Robonaut2 was unpacked, it began initial operation inside the\n       <i>\n        Destiny\n       </i>\n       module for operational testing, but over time, both its location and its applications could expand.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Robonaut2 was initially designed as a prototype to be used on Earth. For its journey to the ISS, R2 received a few upgrades. Outer skin materials were exchanged to meet the ISS\'s strict flammability requirements. Shielding was added to reduce electromagnetic interference and onboard processors were upgraded to increase R2\'s radiation tolerance. The original fans were replaced with quieter ones to accommodate the station\'s restrictive noise environment, and the power system was rewired to run on the station\'s direct current system. Tests were conducted to make sure the robot could both endure the harsh conditions in space and exist in it without doing damage. R2 also underwent vibration testing that simulated the conditions it would experience during its launch onboard\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The robot weighs 300 pounds (140\xc2\xa0kg) and is made out of nickel-plated carbon fiber and aluminum. The height of R2 from waist to head is 3\xc2\xa0feet 3.7\xc2\xa0inches (100.8\xc2\xa0cm), and it has a shoulder width of 2\xc2\xa0feet 7.4\xc2\xa0inches (79.8\xc2\xa0cm). R2 is equipped with 54 servo motors and has 42 degrees of freedom.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Powered by 38\n       <a href="/wiki/PowerPC" title="PowerPC">\n        PowerPC\n       </a>\n       processors, R2\'s systems run at 120 volts DC.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="SpaceX_DragonEye_sensor">\n        SpaceX DragonEye sensor\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: SpaceX DragonEye sensor">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="357" data-file-width="456" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg/220px-DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg/330px-DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg/440px-DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The DragonEye sensor, as seen by an Expedition 26 crew member\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Space Shuttle\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       also carried the Developmental Test Objective (DTO) 701B payload using Advanced Scientific Concepts, Inc.\'s DragonEye 3D Flash light detection and ranging (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LIDAR" title="LIDAR">\n        LIDAR\n       </a>\n       ) sensor. The addition of the pulsed laser navigation sensor was the third time a Space Shuttle provided assistance to the commercial space company\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n        SpaceX\n       </a>\n       , following\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-127" title="STS-127">\n        STS-127\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-129" title="STS-129">\n        STS-129\n       </a>\n       . The DragonEye on STS-133 incorporated several design and software improvements from the version flown on STS-127 to provide increased performance. Its inclusion on STS-133 was part of a final test run ahead of being fully implemented on SpaceX\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_Dragon" title="SpaceX Dragon">\n        Dragon spacecraft\n       </a>\n       , which had its maiden flight in December 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The navigation sensor provides a three-dimensional image based on the time of flight of a single laser pulse from the sensor to the target and back. It provides both range and bearing information from targets that can reflect the light back such as the pressurized mating adapter 2 (PMA2) and those on the station\'s Japanese\n       <i>\n        Kibo\n       </i>\n       laboratory.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The DragonEye DTO was mounted onto\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       \'s existing trajectory control system carrier assembly on the orbiter\'s docking system. SpaceX took data in parallel with\n       <i>\n        Discovery\'\n       </i>\n       s Trajectory Control Sensor (TCS) system. Both the TCS and DragonEye "looked" at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Retroreflector" title="Retroreflector">\n        retroreflectors\n       </a>\n       that are on the station. After the mission, SpaceX compared the data DragonEye collected against the data collected by the TCS to evaluate DragonEye\'s performance.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The sensor was installed onto\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       two weeks later than planned, following a laser rod failure during testing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_items">\n        Other items\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Other items">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       STS-133 carried the signatures of more than 500,000 students who participated in the 2010 Student Signatures in Space program, which was jointly sponsored by NASA and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">\n        Lockheed Martin\n       </a>\n       . The students added their signatures to posters in May 2010 as part of the annual\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Space Day (page does not exist)">\n        Space Day\n       </a>\n       celebration. Through their participation, students also received standards-based lessons that contained a space theme.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2011)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Student Signatures in Space has been active since 1997. In that time, nearly seven million student signatures from 6,552 schools were flown on ten Space Shuttle missions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-signature_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-signature-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Also carried aboard\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       were hundreds of flags, bookmarks and patches which were distributed when the shuttle returned to Earth. The mission also flew two small\n       <a href="/wiki/Lego" title="Lego">\n        Lego\n       </a>\n       Space Shuttles, in honor of an educational partnership between Lego and NASA. Astronauts also carried personal mementos including medallions with connections to their schools or military careers, as well as a\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">\n        William Shakespeare\n       </a>\n       "action figure" from the English Department of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Texas" title="University of Texas">\n        University of Texas\n       </a>\n       , a stuffed giraffe mascot from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memorial_Hermann_Healthcare_System" title="Memorial Hermann Healthcare System">\n        Hermann Children\'s Hospital\n       </a>\n       at the University of Texas, T-shirts from Lomax Junior High School in\n       <a href="/wiki/La_Porte,_Texas" title="La Porte, Texas">\n        La Porte, Texas\n       </a>\n       , a blue\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawaiian_shirt" title="Hawaiian shirt">\n        Hawaiian shirt\n       </a>\n       from NASA\n       <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Space_Center" title="Johnson Space Center">\n        Johnson Space Center\n       </a>\n       \'s Education Office, and a shirt from a\n       <a href="/wiki/Volunteer_fire_department" title="Volunteer fire department">\n        volunteer fire department\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crew">\n        Crew\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Crew">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="wikitable plainrowheaders" style="float: right; margin: 0 0 1em 1em;">\n       <tr>\n        <th style="width:150px;">\n         <a href="/wiki/Astronaut_ranks_and_positions" title="Astronaut ranks and positions">\n          Position\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <th colspan="2" scope="col" style="width:200px;">\n         Astronaut\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crew_18-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Crew-18">\n           [18]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QuickLook1_19-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-QuickLook1-19">\n           [19]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Commander\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <a href="/wiki/Steven_Lindsey" title="Steven Lindsey">\n          Steven Lindsey\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         Fifth and last spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Pilot\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <a href="/wiki/Eric_Boe" title="Eric Boe">\n          Eric Boe\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         Second spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Mission Specialist 1\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Stott" title="Nicole Stott">\n          Nicole Stott\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         Second and last spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Mission Specialist 2\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <a href="/wiki/Alvin_Drew" title="Alvin Drew">\n          Alvin Drew\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         Second and last spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Mission Specialist 3\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <a href="/wiki/Michael_Barratt_(astronaut)" title="Michael Barratt (astronaut)">\n          Michael Barratt\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         Second spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Mission Specialist 4\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Bowen_(astronaut)" title="Stephen Bowen (astronaut)">\n          Stephen Bowen\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         Third spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       NASA announced the STS-133 crew on 18 September 2009, and training began in October 2009. The original crew consisted of commander\n       <a href="/wiki/Steven_Lindsey" title="Steven Lindsey">\n        Steven Lindsey\n       </a>\n       , pilot\n       <a href="/wiki/Eric_Boe" title="Eric Boe">\n        Eric Boe\n       </a>\n       , and mission specialists\n       <a href="/wiki/Alvin_Drew" title="Alvin Drew">\n        Alvin Drew\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Kopra" title="Timothy Kopra">\n        Timothy Kopra\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Barratt_(astronaut)" title="Michael Barratt (astronaut)">\n        Michael Barratt\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Stott" title="Nicole Stott">\n        Nicole Stott\n       </a>\n       . However, on 19 January 2011, about a month before launch, it was announced that\n       <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Bowen_(astronaut)" title="Stephen Bowen (astronaut)">\n        Stephen Bowen\n       </a>\n       would replace original crew member Tim Kopra, after Kopra was injured in a bicycle accident.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-koprareplacement_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-koprareplacement-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       All six crew members had flown at least one spaceflight before; five of the crew members, all but commander Steven Lindsey, were part of NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA_Astronaut_Group_18" title="NASA Astronaut Group 18">\n        Astronaut Group 18\n       </a>\n       , all being selected in the year 2000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The mission commander, Steven Lindsey, handed over his position as\n       <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_Astronaut_Office" title="Chief of the Astronaut Office">\n        Chief of the Astronaut Office\n       </a>\n       position to\n       <a href="/wiki/Peggy_Whitson" title="Peggy Whitson">\n        Peggy Whitson\n       </a>\n       in order to lead the mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133crew_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-133crew-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For the first time, two mission crew members were in space when a crew assignment announcement was made, as Nicole Stott and Michael Barratt were aboard the ISS as part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Expedition_20" title="Expedition 20">\n        Expedition 20\n       </a>\n       crew.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133crew_22-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-133crew-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During STS-133, Alvin Drew became the last\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_African-American_astronauts" title="List of African-American astronauts">\n        African-American astronaut\n       </a>\n       to fly on the Space Shuttle, as no African-Americans were among the crews of\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-134" title="STS-134">\n        STS-134\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-135" title="STS-135">\n        STS-135\n       </a>\n       . Having flown onboard\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">\n        <i>\n         Atlantis\n        </i>\n        \'\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-132" title="STS-132">\n        STS-132\n       </a>\n       mission, Bowen became the first and to date the only NASA astronaut to be launched on two consecutive missions.\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Lindsey, far left, presents a montage to\n           <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">\n            Barack Obama\n           </a>\n           as crew members Barratt, Boe, Stott and Bowen look on.\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_milestones">\n        Mission milestones\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Mission milestones">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The mission marked:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        164th NASA manned space flight\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        133rd shuttle mission since\n        <a href="/wiki/STS-1" title="STS-1">\n         STS-1\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        39th flight of\n        <i>\n         Discovery\n        </i>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        35th shuttle mission to the ISS\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        108th post-\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">\n          Challenger\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        mission\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        20th post-\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">\n          Columbia\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        mission\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crew_training">\n        Crew training\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Crew training">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_countdown_demonstration_test">\n        Terminal countdown demonstration test\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Terminal countdown demonstration test">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       On 12 October 2010, the STS-133 crew arrived at the Kennedy Space Center to conduct the Terminal Countdown Demonstration Test (TCDT). The TCDT consisted of training for both the crew and the launch team that simulated the final hours up until launch. During the TCDT, the crew went through a number of exercises that included rescue training and a launch day simulation that included everything that would happen on launch day \xe2\x80\x93 except the launch. Commander Steve Lindsey and Pilot Eric Boe also performed abort landings and other flight aspects in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Shuttle_Training_Aircraft" title="Shuttle Training Aircraft">\n        Shuttle Training Aircraft\n       </a>\n       (STA). For the TCDT, the crew also received a briefing from NASA engineers, outlining the work that had been carried out on\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       during the STS-133 processing flow. After successfully completing all the TCDT tasks, the crew returned to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Space_Center" title="Johnson Space Center">\n        Johnson Space Center\n       </a>\n       on 15 October 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vapor_leak_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-vapor_leak-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Flying aboard NASA\n       <a href="/wiki/Northrop_T-38_Talon" title="Northrop T-38 Talon">\n        T-38 training jets\n       </a>\n       , the six astronauts returned to Kennedy Space Center on 28 October 2010 for final pre-launch preparations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-133_Crew_Begins_Dress_Rehearsal.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="1996" data-file-width="3000" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/STS-133_Crew_Begins_Dress_Rehearsal.jpg/120px-STS-133_Crew_Begins_Dress_Rehearsal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/STS-133_Crew_Begins_Dress_Rehearsal.jpg/180px-STS-133_Crew_Begins_Dress_Rehearsal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/STS-133_Crew_Begins_Dress_Rehearsal.jpg/240px-STS-133_Crew_Begins_Dress_Rehearsal.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           The crew gathered for the Terminal Countdown Demonstration Test.\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Launch_Pad_39A_during_the_Terminal_Countdown_Demonstration_Test_for_STS-133.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3000" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Launch_Pad_39A_during_the_Terminal_Countdown_Demonstration_Test_for_STS-133.jpg/120px-Launch_Pad_39A_during_the_Terminal_Countdown_Demonstration_Test_for_STS-133.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Launch_Pad_39A_during_the_Terminal_Countdown_Demonstration_Test_for_STS-133.jpg/180px-Launch_Pad_39A_during_the_Terminal_Countdown_Demonstration_Test_for_STS-133.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Launch_Pad_39A_during_the_Terminal_Countdown_Demonstration_Test_for_STS-133.jpg/240px-Launch_Pad_39A_during_the_Terminal_Countdown_Demonstration_Test_for_STS-133.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">\n            Launch Pad 39A\n           </a>\n           during the Terminal Countdown Demonstration Test.\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       On 15 January 2011, Timothy Kopra, scheduled as the lead spacewalker for the mission at the time, was injured in a bicycle accident near his\n       <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">\n        Houston\n       </a>\n       -area home, reportedly breaking his\n       <a href="/wiki/Hip" title="Hip">\n        hip\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sub_for_Kopra_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Sub_for_Kopra-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       He was replaced by Stephen Bowen on 19 January 2011. The replacement did not affect the targeted launch date.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-koprareplacement_20-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-koprareplacement-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This is to date the closest to a scheduled launch that a Space Shuttle crewmember has been replaced. During the\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">\n        Apollo program\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jack_Swigert" title="Jack Swigert">\n        Jack Swigert\n       </a>\n       replaced\n       <a href="/wiki/Ken_Mattingly" title="Ken Mattingly">\n        Ken Mattingly\n       </a>\n       three days prior to the launch of\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_13" title="Apollo 13">\n        Apollo 13\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sub_for_Kopra_25-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Sub_for_Kopra-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Shuttle_processing">\n        Shuttle processing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Shuttle processing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       STS-133 was originally manifested for launch on 16 September 2010. In June 2010 the launch date was moved to the end of October 2010 and the mission was set to take place before STS-134, which in turn had been rescheduled to February 2011. STS-133 had the longest vertical flow period (170 days) since\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-35" title="STS-35">\n        STS-35\n       </a>\n       (185 days).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       was moved from its hangar in the Orbiter Processing Facility (OPF)-3 to the nearby 52-story\n       <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">\n        Vehicle Assembly Building\n       </a>\n       (VAB) on 9 September 2010. The shuttle emerged from OPF-3 at 06:54 EDT and the rollover was done at 10:46 EDT when\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       came to a rest in the VAB\'s transfer aisle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The quarter-mile trip between the OPF-3 and VAB was the 41st rollover for Discovery. The rollover was originally planned at 06:30 EDT on 8 September 2010. The move did not commence due to the unavailability of fire suppression systems because of a broken water main near the VAB and turn basin that runs out to the shuttle launch pads.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The two SRBs were designated as flight set 122 by contractor\n       <a href="/wiki/Alliant_Techsystems" title="Alliant Techsystems">\n        Alliant Techsystems\n       </a>\n       and were made up from one new segment and remaining segments reused across 54 earlier shuttle missions dating back to\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-1" title="STS-1">\n        STS-1\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-srb_use_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-srb_use-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Inside the VAB, engineers attached a large sling to\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       and the orbiter was rotated vertical. The orbiter was lifted into the high bay where its external tank (ET-137) and boosters were waiting to be mated. During the mating operations, an internal nut pre-positioned inside the aft compartment of the orbiter slipped out of position and fell away inside the compartment.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Engineers initially were worried that the orbiter would have to be removed from the ET and placed back in a horizontal orientation to make repairs. However, later they successfully accessed the area inside the aft compartment, and re-positioned the nut to complete the repairs. The bolting of the orbiter to its ET (\'hard mate\') was completed early in the morning of 11 September 2010 at 09:27 EDT.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The shuttle\'s 44th rollout to the launch pad was scheduled to begin at 20:00 EDT on 20 September 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NASA sent out more than 700 invitations to shuttle workers so they could bring their families to watch Discovery\'s journey to the pad. However, the shuttle began the 3.4 mile trek from the VAB to the pad earlier than planned at about at 19:23 EDT on 20 September 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       took about six hours to arrive at Pad 39A. The shuttle was secured on the launch pad by 01:49 EDT the next day.\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Discovery_High_Bay_3_Vehicle_Assembly_Building_STS-133.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Discovery_High_Bay_3_Vehicle_Assembly_Building_STS-133.jpg/120px-Discovery_High_Bay_3_Vehicle_Assembly_Building_STS-133.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Discovery_High_Bay_3_Vehicle_Assembly_Building_STS-133.jpg/180px-Discovery_High_Bay_3_Vehicle_Assembly_Building_STS-133.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Discovery_High_Bay_3_Vehicle_Assembly_Building_STS-133.jpg/240px-Discovery_High_Bay_3_Vehicle_Assembly_Building_STS-133.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           <small>\n            <i>\n             Discovery\n            </i>\n            being lowered onto its external fuel tank and solid rocket boosters in High Bay 3 of the Vehicle Assembly Building.\n           </small>\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:33.5px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Discovery_at_Launch_Pad_(STS0133).jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2069" data-file-width="3000" height="83" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Discovery_at_Launch_Pad_%28STS0133%29.jpg/120px-Discovery_at_Launch_Pad_%28STS0133%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Discovery_at_Launch_Pad_%28STS0133%29.jpg/180px-Discovery_at_Launch_Pad_%28STS0133%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Discovery_at_Launch_Pad_%28STS0133%29.jpg/240px-Discovery_at_Launch_Pad_%28STS0133%29.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Space Shuttle\n           <i>\n            Discovery\n           </i>\n           attached to Launch Pad 39A on 21 September 2010.\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-133_Discovery_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/STS-133_Discovery_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg/120px-STS-133_Discovery_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/STS-133_Discovery_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg/180px-STS-133_Discovery_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/STS-133_Discovery_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg/240px-STS-133_Discovery_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Discovery at Launch Pad 39A on 1 February 2011.\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS_133_Discovery_KSC_After_RSS_Roll_Back.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2465" data-file-width="3704" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/STS_133_Discovery_KSC_After_RSS_Roll_Back.jpg/120px-STS_133_Discovery_KSC_After_RSS_Roll_Back.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/STS_133_Discovery_KSC_After_RSS_Roll_Back.jpg/180px-STS_133_Discovery_KSC_After_RSS_Roll_Back.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/STS_133_Discovery_KSC_After_RSS_Roll_Back.jpg/240px-STS_133_Discovery_KSC_After_RSS_Roll_Back.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Discovery is seen shortly after the\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rotating_Service_Structure" title="Rotating Service Structure">\n            Rotating Service Structure\n           </a>\n           was rolled back on 23 February 2011.\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Orbital_Maneuvering_System_vapor_leak">\n        Orbital Maneuvering System vapor leak\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Orbital Maneuvering System vapor leak">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       On 14 October 2010, engineers at the launch pad first discovered a small leak in a propellant line for\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       \'s orbital maneuvering system (OMS) engines. The leak was detected after they noticed a fishy smell coming from the aft of the shuttle, thought of as a sign of fuel vapor in the air.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vapor_leak_23-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-vapor_leak-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Upon inspection, the leak was found at a flange located at the interface where two propellant lines met in\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       \'s aft compartment. The line carried\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monomethyl_hydrazine" title="Monomethyl hydrazine">\n        monomethyl hydrazine\n       </a>\n       (MMH) propellant, one of two chemicals (the other is an oxidizer,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nitrogen_tetroxide" title="Nitrogen tetroxide">\n        nitrogen tetroxide\n       </a>\n       ) used to ignite the OMS engines. Engineers replaced an Air Half Coupling (AHC) flight cap. However, the new cap failed to solve the problem since vapor checks still showed signs of a leak. An aspirator was activated to collect the vapor at the leak-site allowing work to continue in other locations around the aft segment of\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It was believed that the leak was in the crossfeed flange area \xe2\x80\x93 a problem with associated seals. On 18 October 2010, after an afternoon review, engineers were asked to double-check the torque on six bolts around the suspected leaky flange fitting and tighten if necessary.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Subsequent leak tests showed again signs of seepage, and the task of solving the issue required the draining of both the left and right OMS tanks of the shuttle and a unique in-situ repair at the pad to avoid a rollback.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 23 October 2010, engineers completed the removal and replacement of the two seals on the right OMS crossfeed flange, after the education (a vacuum-related procedure, used to completely clear the plumbing of the toxic MMH) of the plumbing was completed ahead of the schedule by over a day.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Later, testing indicated that the new seals were properly seated and holding pressure with no signs of additional seepage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Normal pad operations commenced soon after allowing managers to press forward with the confirmation of a 1 November 2010 target launch date, with fuel reloading into the OMS tanks beginning on the morning of 24 October 2010.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Main_engine_controller_problem">\n        Main engine controller problem\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Main engine controller problem">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       On 2 November, while readying\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       for launch, engineers reported an electrical issue on the backup Main Engine Controller (MEC) mounted on Engine No. 3 (SSME-3). Earlier in the morning, engineers said that the problem had been solved, however another glitch in the system raised concerns and additional troubleshooting was ordered. Troubleshooting followed and indicated the problem was related to "transient contamination" in a circuit breaker. NASA Test Director Steve Payne, addressing reporters, told that after troubleshooting and power cycles, the controller powered up normally. However, at the same time the problem was thought to be a non-issue, an unexpected voltage drop was observed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In a Mission Management Team (MMT) meeting held later that day, managers decided to scrub the launch for at least 24 hours to work towards flight rationale.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_Umbilical_Carrier_Plate_leak">\n        Ground Umbilical Carrier Plate leak\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ground Umbilical Carrier Plate leak">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS_133_GUCP_Quick_Disconnect_removal.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/STS_133_GUCP_Quick_Disconnect_removal.jpg/220px-STS_133_GUCP_Quick_Disconnect_removal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/STS_133_GUCP_Quick_Disconnect_removal.jpg/330px-STS_133_GUCP_Quick_Disconnect_removal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/STS_133_GUCP_Quick_Disconnect_removal.jpg/440px-STS_133_GUCP_Quick_Disconnect_removal.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS_133_GUCP_Quick_Disconnect_removal.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A technician begins to remove the leaky GUCP\'s quick disconnect.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On 5 November 2010,\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       \'s launch attempt, a hydrogen leak was detected at the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ground_Umbilical_Carrier_Plate" title="Ground Umbilical Carrier Plate">\n        Ground Umbilical Carrier Plate\n       </a>\n       (GUCP) during the fueling process. The plate was an attachment point between the external tank and a 17-inch pipe that carried gaseous hydrogen safely away from the tank to the flare stack, where it was burned off. All had been proceeding to plan with the tank "fast filled" during tanking, until the first leak indication was revealed. Firstly, a 33,000 ppm leak then reduced to a level below 20,000 ppm was recorded. The Launch Commit Criteria limit was 40\xe2\x80\x9344,000 ppm. The leak was only being observed during the cycling of the vent valve to "open" to release the gaseous hydrogen from the tank to the flare stack. Controllers decided to stop valve cycling in order to increase the pressure and attempt to force a seal before attempting to complete the fast fill process. At this stage, the leak spiked and remained at the highest 60,000 ppm level (likely even at a higher value), indicating a serious problem with the GUCP\'s seal.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Shuttle launch director Mike Leinbach characterized the leak as "significant," similar to what was seen on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-119" title="STS-119">\n        STS-119\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-127" title="STS-127">\n        STS-127\n       </a>\n       , although the rate was higher in magnitude and occurred earlier in the fueling process.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS_133_gucp_replacement.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2000" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/STS_133_gucp_replacement.jpg/160px-STS_133_gucp_replacement.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/STS_133_gucp_replacement.jpg/240px-STS_133_gucp_replacement.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/STS_133_gucp_replacement.jpg/320px-STS_133_gucp_replacement.jpg 2x" width="160"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS_133_gucp_replacement.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Technicians begin to install a new GUCP on the external tank.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       After the day required to make the tank safe by purging remaining hydrogen gas with helium gas, NASA engineers prepared for disconnection of the vent arm and the significant number of lines prior to taking their first look at the GUCP. On the night of 9 November, technicians began disconnecting the GUCP by unhooking and lowering the hydrogen vent line. Teams performed an initial inspection of the flight seal and quick disconnect prior to sending them to labs for a thorough engineering analysis. Engineers reported an unevenly (asymmetrically) compressed internal seal and the quick disconnect hardware also seemed have a less concentric fit than pre-fueling measurements indicated.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Inspections also confirmed the condition of the hardware did not match the observations documented when it was installed on the external tank inside the VAB.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On the morning of 12 November, teams began installing a new GUCP and completed the GUCP work over the next two days. The new plate was previously fit checked on the external tank at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Michoud_Assembly_Facility" title="Michoud Assembly Facility">\n        Michoud Assembly Facility\n       </a>\n       and yielded substantially better concentricity values than was obtained with the old and removed GUCP. Technicians took extra measurements to ensure the best possible alignment of the newly installed GUCP. Teams began installing the flight seal and quick disconnect on 15 November.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cracks_in_the_external_tank">\n        Cracks in the external tank\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cracks in the external tank">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-133crack.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="523" data-file-width="398" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/STS-133crack.jpg/120px-STS-133crack.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/STS-133crack.jpg/180px-STS-133crack.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/STS-133crack.jpg/240px-STS-133crack.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-133crack.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         structural cracks in external fuel tank\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-133_intertank_section_foam_crack.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1280" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/STS-133_intertank_section_foam_crack.jpg/220px-STS-133_intertank_section_foam_crack.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/STS-133_intertank_section_foam_crack.jpg/330px-STS-133_intertank_section_foam_crack.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/STS-133_intertank_section_foam_crack.jpg/440px-STS-133_intertank_section_foam_crack.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-133_intertank_section_foam_crack.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Intertank section foam crack.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS133_technicians_spray_foam_on_the_tank.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1001" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/STS133_technicians_spray_foam_on_the_tank.jpg/220px-STS133_technicians_spray_foam_on_the_tank.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/STS133_technicians_spray_foam_on_the_tank.jpg/330px-STS133_technicians_spray_foam_on_the_tank.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/STS133_technicians_spray_foam_on_the_tank.jpg/440px-STS133_technicians_spray_foam_on_the_tank.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS133_technicians_spray_foam_on_the_tank.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Technicians spray foam insulation on a section of repaired stringers.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Additional inspection of the tank revealed cracks in foam insulation in the flange between the intertank and liquid oxygen tank. The cracks are believed to have occurred about an hour after super-cold propellants began flowing into the external tank for the 5 November launch attempt. The cracks in the tank were the first to be found at the launch pad.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The insulation was cut away for additional inspection, revealing two additional 9-inch metal cracks on either side of an underlying structural rib called "stringer S-7-2". NASA managers then decided to cut away additional foam and observed two more cracks on a stringer known as S-6-2 adjacent to the two original cracks. They were found on the far left of removed foam on the flange area between the intertank and the liquid oxygen tank. However, these cracks appeared to have suffered less stress than the others found.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       No cracks were found in stringers on the right side. NASA suspected the use of a lightweight aluminum-lithium alloy in the tanks contributed to the crack problem. Repairs commenced while the shuttle remained on the pad.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An environmental enclosure was erected around the known damage site to facilitate the ongoing repairs and eventually to apply fresh foam insulation. On 18 November, as part of the repairs, technicians installed new sections of metal, called "doublers" because they are twice as thick as the original stringer metal providing additional strength, to replace the two cracked stringers on\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       \'s external tank.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Scanning of the stringers on the liquid oxygen/intertank flange was completed on 23 November.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NASA also performed\n       <a href="/wiki/Backscatter" title="Backscatter">\n        backscatter\n       </a>\n       scanning of the lower liquid hydrogen/intertank flange stringers on 29 November.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Program managers identified the analysis and repairs that were required to safely launch the shuttle, and this analysis was reviewed at a special Program Requirements Control Board (PRCB) held on 24 November. Managers announced at that meeting that the launch window available in early December would be passed up, with a new target of 17 December set, but cautioned that the launch could slip into February 2011. After reviewing the space station\'s December traffic model following the realigned\n       <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler_ATV" title="Johannes Kepler ATV">\n        Johannes Kepler ATV\n       </a>\n       \'s launch date, NASA had identified a potential launch window in mid-/late-December 2010. The 17 December 2010 date was preferred because it would have allowed the shuttle to carry more stored oxygen to the International Space Station to help it deal with oxygen generation issues, which the crew had dealt with for several months.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       "What we\'ve told the agency leadership is that clearly we\'re not ready for the 3 December to 7 December window that\'s coming up next week," John Shannon, NASA\'s SSP manager, said in a news conference held after the special PCRB. "We\'ll leave the option open for a launch window for 17 December, but a lot of data has to come together to support that".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Johannes_Kepler_ATV_rescheduled">\n        Johannes Kepler ATV rescheduled\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Johannes Kepler ATV rescheduled">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The launch date of 24 February 2011 was officially set after the Flight Readiness Review meeting on 18 February 2011. Reviews of previous problems, including the GUP vent line connection, external tank foam and external tank stringer cracks, were found to be positive. Additionally, flight rules which required a 72-hour separation between dockings at the International Space Station threatened to delay the launch by at least a day due to the delayed launch of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESA" title="ESA">\n        ESA\n       </a>\n       \'s unmanned\n       <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler_ATV" title="Johannes Kepler ATV">\n        Johannes Kepler ATV\n       </a>\n       supply craft. Managers instead decided to press ahead with the countdown allowing for a possible standdown; had docking issues arisen with the ATV, STS-133 would have stood down for 48 hours.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Kepler ATV docked successfully at 10:59 UTC, 24 February 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasatv_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nasatv-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_attempts">\n        Launch attempts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-133&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Launch attempts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <i>\n         <small>\n          All times Eastern Time, first 5 are while daylight saving time was in effect (EDT), attempt 6 is during outside of daylight saving (EST). Because of this, the final "turnaround" category should be 111 days,\n          <b>\n           2 hours\n          </b>\n          , 49 minutes, it is not due to automatic formatting.\n
